- **Sintering Time**: 12 hours is a reasonable duration to ensure complete reaction and proper densification of the material.
- **Calcination Temperature**: 850°C is selected to decompose any remaining carbonates and to initiate the formation of the desired phase without causing excessive grain growth.
- **Calcination Time**: 8 hours is sufficient to ensure complete decomposition of carbonates and initial phase formation.

### Explanation:
- **Sintering Temperature (1350°C)**: This temperature is chosen to ensure complete reaction and formation of the MgNb2O6 phase. It is within the typical range for similar oxide reactions.
- **Sintering Time (10 hours)**: This duration allows for sufficient time for the reaction to go to completion and for the formation of a dense and homogeneous product.
- **Calcination Temperature (1100°C)**: This temperature is used to remove any residual organics or impurities and to promote initial phase formation before sintering.
- **Calcination Time (5 hours)**: This duration is sufficient to ensure complete decomposition of any carbonates and initial phase formation.
